{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_018Cu7nTkgYhSrVEwd178Gto","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01MnmibP8gPKXWYUSXYjLYZx","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Kubelet Container Manager Architecture Guide\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Scope\n\nThe **Container Manager (CM)** subsystem is responsible for managing containerized workloads on a Kubernetes node. It serves as the authoritative interface between the kubelet and the underlying container runtime infrastructure, enforcing resource constraints, managing cgroup hierarchies, and coordinating resource allocation across CPUs, memory, and specialized devices.\n\n### Core Responsibilities\n\n- **Container Lifecycle Management**: Coordinate container creation, starting, stopping, and removal through the container runtime\n- **Resource Enforcement**: Apply CPU, memory, and device limits via cgroups (v1 and v2)\n- **QoS Hierarchy**: Implement Kubernetes QoS classes (Guaranteed, Burstable, BestEffort) using cgroup hierarchies\n- **Node Allocatable**: Reserve resources for system daemons and kubelet itself\n- **Resource Coordination**: Orchestrate allocation decisions across CPU manager, memory manager, device manager, and topology manager\n- **Health Checking**: Monitor device plugins and report resource health status\n\n### Boundaries and Upstream/Downstream Dependencies\n\n**Upstream Dependencies (Callers):**\n- **Kubelet (`pkg/kubelet/kubelet.go`)**: Calls CM to initialize, manage pod lifecycle, and enforce node allocatable\n- **Pod Workers (`pkg/kubelet/pod_workers.go`)**: Requests container runtime operations via CM\n- **Lifecycle Hooks**: Pod admission handlers and resource allocation triggers\n- **API Server**: Provides pod and node specifications\n\n**Downstream Dependencies (Consumers):**\n- **Container Runtime Interface (CRI)**: gRPC service for container/sandbox operations\n- **cgroup Filesystem**: Linux kernel interface for resource enforcement\n- **Device Plugins**: Kubernetes device plugin protocol for custom resources\n- **OOM Killer & Kernel**: Linux kernel mechanisms for resource enforcement and OOM handling\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 Core Container Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/`)\n\n**Main Interface: `ContainerManager` (`container_manager.go:66-170`)**\n\nThe primary abstraction defining the contract for all CM operations:\n\n```\ntype ContainerManager interface {\n    Start()                              // Initialize and verify system state\n    SystemCgroupsLimit()                 // Reserve resources for system\n    GetNodeConfig()                      // Access configuration\n    NewPodContainerManager()             // Factory for pod-level cgroup manager\n    GetResources()                       // Resolve extended resources for pods\n    InternalContainerLifecycle()         // Register lifecycle hooks\n    GetPluginRegistrationHandlers()      // Support device plugin discovery\n    UpdateQOSCgroups()                   // Periodic housekeeping\n    GetCapacity()                        // Report node capacity\n    GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()// Pod admission hook\n    PrepareDynamicResources()            // DRA resource preparation\n    // ... and many more methods\n}\n```\n\n**Implementation: `containerManagerImpl` (`container_manager_linux.go:100-140`)**\n\nThe Linux-specific implementation holding:\n\n- **cgroup manager** (`cgroupManager CgroupManager`): Manages cgroup hierarchy creation/updates via systemd or cgroupfs\n- **Resource managers**: CPU, memory, device, topology, and DRA managers\n- **QoS container manager** (`qosContainerManager QOSContainerManager`): Maintains Guaranteed/Burstable/BestEffort hierarchy\n- **Periodic tasks**: Background jobs for reconciliation and enforcement\n\n### 2.2 cgroup Management (`pkg/kubelet/cm/`)\n\n**Cgroup Manager Interface (`types.go:62-97`)**\n\nAbstracts cgroup operations:\n\n```\ntype CgroupManager interface {\n    Create()              // Create cgroup with resource limits\n    Destroy()             // Remove cgroup\n    Update()              // Modify resource limits\n    Exists()              // Check cgroup presence\n    GetCgroupConfig()     // Read applied resource config\n    MemoryUsage()         // Query current memory consumption\n    Pids()                // List processes in cgroup\n    ReduceCPULimits()     // Hard-cap CPU shares\n    Version()             // Return cgroup version (1 or 2)\n}\n```\n\n**cgroup Hierarchy Structure:**\n\n```\n/ (root)\n├── system.slice/          (--system-reserved-cgroups)\n├── kubepods.slice/        (Pod cgroup root, --pod-cgroup-root)\n│   ├── guaranteed/        (Guaranteed QoS class)\n│   │   └── pod<uid>/      (Individual pods)\n│   │       ├── <container> (Actual containers)\n│   ├── burstable/         (Burstable QoS class)\n│   │   └── pod<uid>/\n│   └── besteffort/        (BestEffort QoS class)\n│       └── pod<uid>/\n└── docker/                (System container for kubelet)\n    └── <pid> -> actual kubelet process\n```\n\n**Cgroup Versions (v1 vs v2):**\n- **v1** (`cgroup_manager_linux.go`): Separate hierarchies per resource type (cpu, memory, cpuset)\n- **v2** (`cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go`): Unified hierarchy with unified cgroup config\n- Detected at runtime; v1 deprecated (see warning at `container_manager.go:52`)\n\n### 2.3 Resource Managers\n\n#### CPU Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/`)\n\n**Purpose**: Allocate exclusive CPUs for latency-sensitive workloads.\n\n**Key Methods** (`cpu_manager.go:55-103`):\n- `Allocate()`: Pre-allocate CPUs at pod admission time\n- `AddContainer()`: Register container after creation; apply CPU affinity\n- `RemoveContainer()`: Free CPUs when container stops\n- `GetTopologyHints()`: Provide NUMA affinity preferences\n- `GetExclusiveCPUs()`: Query assigned CPUs (PodResources API)\n\n**Policies**:\n- **none** (`policy_none.go`): No CPU affinity; shared pool\n- **static** (`policy_static.go`): Exclusive CPU allocation for QoS=Guaranteed pods; others share\n- Policy state stored in `cpu_manager_state` file under kubelet root dir\n\n#### Memory Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/`)\n\n**Purpose**: Allocate memory from specific NUMA nodes (memory affinity).\n\n**Key Methods** (`memory_manager.go:57-95`):\n- `Allocate()`: Pre-allocate memory at pod admission\n- `AddContainer()`: Apply NUMA memory binding after container creation\n- `RemoveContainer()`: Release NUMA memory reservation\n- `GetTopologyHints()`: Provide NUMA affinity preferences\n- `GetMemoryNUMANodes()`: Query assigned NUMA nodes\n\n**Policies**:\n- **none**: No NUMA affinity; memory from any node\n- **static**: Reserve memory from specific NUMA nodes; allocate from reserved pools\n- State stored in `memory_manager_state` file\n\n#### Device Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/`)\n\n**Purpose**: Manage extended resources (GPUs, NICs) provided by device plugins.\n\n**Key Components** (`manager.go:61-100`):\n- **endpoints**: Tracks registered device plugins\n- **allocatedDevices**: Per-pod device allocations\n- **topologyAffinityStore**: NUMA topology for devices\n- **checkpointManager**: Persists allocation state\n\n**Workflow**:\n1. Device plugin registers via Unix socket\n2. Plugin reports available device IDs\n3. Kubelet allocates devices to pods (Allocate() call)\n4. Device manager returns device env vars, mounts, and CDI devices\n5. Kubelet passes these to container runtime\n\n#### Topology Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/`)\n\n**Purpose**: Coordinate resource affinity across CPU, memory, and device managers.\n\n**Key Concepts**:\n- **Scopes**: pod (single pod) or container (per-container)\n- **Policies**: none, best-effort, restricted, single-numa-node\n- **Hint Provider Interface**: CPU, memory, device managers implement to provide topology hints\n- **Affinity Resolution**: Merges hints from all providers to find best NUMA node set\n\n**Flow**:\n1. Pod admission triggers topology manager's PodAdmitHandler\n2. Queries all hint providers (CPU, memory, device managers)\n3. Merges hints to find consensus best affinity\n4. Stores affinity result; providers retrieve via GetAffinity()\n5. Providers allocate resources accordingly\n\n#### DRA Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/`)\n\n**Purpose**: Manage Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) claims and per-node resources.\n\n**Integration**: Manages allocation of DRAClaims to pods; coordinates with device manager.\n\n### 2.4 Pod Container Management (`pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_*.go`)\n\n**Interface: `PodContainerManager` (`types.go:106-141`)**\n\nManages pod-level cgroup containers (when QoS hierarchy enabled):\n\n```\ntype PodContainerManager interface {\n    GetPodContainerName()           // Get cgroup name for pod\n    EnsureExists()                  // Create pod cgroup if needed\n    Exists()                        // Check pod cgroup presence\n    Destroy()                       // Remove pod cgroup\n    GetAllPodsFromCgroups()         // Enumerate existing pods\n    IsPodCgroup()                   // Identify if path is pod cgroup\n    GetPodCgroupMemoryUsage()       // Query memory consumption\n    // ... and others\n}\n```\n\n**Implementation: `podContainerManagerImpl` (when `--cgroups-per-qos=true`)**\n- Creates pod-level cgroups under QoS class containers\n- Applies CPU, memory, and PID limits based on pod requests\n- Enforces memory QoS limits (cgroup v2 only)\n\n**Fallback: `podContainerManagerNoop` (when `--cgroups-per-qos=false`)**\n- No-op implementation; pods share QoS class cgroups\n\n### 2.5 QoS Container Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_linux.go`)\n\n**Purpose**: Create and manage top-level QoS class cgroup hierarchy.\n\n**Initialization** (`qos_container_manager_linux.go:84-130`):\n1. Creates three top-level cgroup containers:\n   - `kubepods/guaranteed` (for Guaranteed pods)\n   - `kubepods/burstable` (for Burstable pods)\n   - `kubepods/besteffort` (for BestEffort pods)\n2. Sets CPU shares and memory limits based on node allocatable\n3. Periodic reconciliation via `UpdateCgroups()`\n\n### 2.6 Internal Container Lifecycle (`pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go`)\n\n**Purpose**: Hook container lifecycle events to resource managers.\n\n**Methods** (`internal_container_lifecycle.go:28-57`):\n\n```\ntype InternalContainerLifecycle interface {\n    PreCreateContainer()   // Before runtime creates container\n    PreStartContainer()    // Before container starts (after creation)\n    PostStopContainer()    // After container stops\n}\n```\n\n**Implementation** (`internalContainerLifecycleImpl`):\n- `PreStartContainer()`: Calls CPU and memory managers' AddContainer()\n- `PostStopContainer()`: Calls topology manager's RemoveContainer()\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### 3.1 Container Manager Initialization (`container_manager_linux.go:615-650+`)\n\n**Entry Point**: `containerManagerImpl.Start()` (kubelet startup)\n\n**Sequence**:\n\n```\nStart(ctx, node, activePods, getNode, sourcesReady, podStatusProvider, runtimeService)\n  ↓\n1. buildContainerMapAndRunningSetFromRuntime()\n   - Query runtime for existing containers\n   - Build map of active containers before kubelet restart\n\n2. setupNode()\n   - Validate cgroup subsystems available\n   - Check kernel tunables (VM overcommit, panic on OOM, etc.)\n   - Create node allocatable cgroup if --cgroups-per-qos=true\n   - Start QOS container manager\n   - Set up system containers (system.slice, docker)\n\n3. Start DRA manager (if DynamicResourceAllocation feature enabled)\n\n4. Start CPU manager\n   - Initialize CPU topology from cAdvisor\n   - Load persisted state from cpu_manager_state\n   - Start reconciliation goroutine\n\n5. Start memory manager\n   - Load persisted state from memory_manager_state\n   - Initialize NUMA node mapping\n   - Start reconciliation goroutine\n\n6. Create unified resource updates channel\n   - Fan-in device manager and DRA manager updates\n   - Kubelet main loop consumes this channel\n\n7. Register device manager as hint provider with topology manager\n8. Register CPU manager as hint provider with topology manager\n9. Register memory manager as hint provider with topology manager\n```\n\n### 3.2 Pod Admission and Resource Allocation\n\n**Entry Point**: Pod created in API server → kubelet watches → pod workers process\n\n**Sequence**:\n\n```\nkubelet.podWorkers.UpdatePod(pod)\n  ↓\nGenerateAPIPodStatus()\n  ↓\ncontainerManager.UpdatePluginResources()\n  - Call device manager to update node allocatable with device plugin resources\n  ↓\ncontainerManager.GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()\n  ↓\nhandler.Admit(pod)\n  ↓\ntopologyManager.Admit(pod)\n  ↓\nFor each container in pod:\n  1. cpuManager.GetTopologyHints()     → {cpu: [numa0:true, numa1:false]}\n  2. memoryManager.GetTopologyHints()  → {memory: [numa0:true, numa1:false]}\n  3. deviceManager.GetTopologyHints()  → {gpu: [numa0:true]}\n  ↓\n  Merge hints → {numa0: preferred}\n  ↓\n4. cpuManager.Allocate(pod, container)\n   - If static policy + QoS=Guaranteed:\n     - Reserve exclusive CPUs from cpuManager.cpuset\n     - Save to state file\n   - Else: shared pool (no pre-allocation)\n\n5. memoryManager.Allocate(pod, container)\n   - If static policy + sufficient memory on preferred NUMA:\n     - Reserve memory from that node's pool\n     - Save to state file\n   - Else: no NUMA affinity\n\n6. deviceManager.Allocate(pod)\n   - Call device plugin's Allocate() RPC\n   - Device plugin returns device IDs and mount/env info\n   - Save allocation to checkpoint\n```\n\n### 3.3 Container Creation and Start\n\n**Entry Point**: Pod sync in pod worker\n\n**Sequence**:\n\n```\nkuberuntime_manager.SyncPod(pod, ...)\n  ↓\nFor each init/regular container:\n\n1. kuberuntime_container.createContainer()\n   ↓\n   containerManager.GetResources(pod, container)\n   - Topology manager returns selected NUMA affinity\n   - CPU manager returns exclusive CPUs (if any)\n   - Memory manager returns NUMA memory binding\n   - Device manager returns mounts, env, CDI devices\n   - Return RunContainerOptions with all above\n   ↓\n   runtimeService.CreateContainer(config)\n   - Include RunContainerOptions in CRI request\n   - Runtime (containerd/CRI-O) creates sandbox/container with cgroups\n\n2. containerManager.InternalContainerLifecycle().PreStartContainer()\n   ↓\n   cpuManager.AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n   - Apply CPU affinity via UpdateContainerResources() RPC\n   - If exclusive CPUs: TaskSet the container\n   - Record in cpuManager state\n   ↓\n   memoryManager.AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n   - Apply NUMA memory binding\n   - Record in memoryManager state\n   ↓\n   topologyManager.AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n   - Store affinity → enable future queries via PodResources API\n\n3. runtimeService.StartContainer(containerID)\n   - Container actually runs with applied resource constraints\n```\n\n### 3.4 Container Cleanup\n\n**Entry Point**: Pod deletion or container failure\n\n**Sequence**:\n\n```\nkuberuntime_manager.KillPod() or KillContainer()\n  ↓\nruntimeService.StopContainer(containerID)\n  - Container stops\n\ncontainerManager.InternalContainerLifecycle().PostStopContainer()\n  ↓\ntopologyManager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n  - Forget topology affinity\n\n(No explicit CPU/memory manager cleanup; tracked via containerID)\n\ncpuManager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n  - Free exclusive CPUs\n  - Update cpuManager state\n\nmemoryManager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n  - Free NUMA memory reservation\n  - Update memoryManager state\n\ndeviceManager tracks containers and cleans up on pod deletion\n  - Update checkpoint file\n```\n\n### 3.5 Periodic Reconciliation\n\n**Triggered by**: Timer in each resource manager\n\n**CPU Manager Reconciliation** (default 5s):\n```\ncpuManager.reconcileState()\n  ↓\n1. Get list of active pods from kubelet\n2. Compare with cpuManager state\n3. For containers no longer in active pods:\n   - Remove from state\n   - Free CPUs\n4. For containers in state but not in runtime:\n   - Try to recover via runtime.GetContainers()\n5. For containers with wrong CPU affinity:\n   - Call UpdateContainerResources() to fix\n6. Save state to disk\n```\n\n**Memory Manager Reconciliation** (similar pattern):\n```\nmemoryManager.reconcileState()\n  ↓\n1. Validate allocations against runtime containers\n2. Free allocations for dead pods\n3. Save state to disk\n```\n\n**QoS Manager Reconciliation** (default 1 minute):\n```\nqosContainerManager.UpdateCgroups()\n  ↓\n1. Recompute expected CPU/memory for each QoS class\n2. Get list of active pods in each QoS class\n3. Update cgroup limits to match current allocation + reserved\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Failure Modes\n\n#### CPU Allocation Conflicts\n- **Scenario**: Pod with `requests.cpu` exceeds allocatable non-reserved CPUs\n- **Detection**: cpuManager.Allocate() fails during pod admission\n- **Behavior**: Pod rejected; user sees \"Insufficient cpu\" error\n- **Recovery**: User must reduce pod CPU request or add more nodes\n\n#### Memory Allocation Failures\n- **Scenario**: Pod with NUMA memory affinity but all NUMA nodes exhausted\n- **Detection**: memoryManager.Allocate() fails during pod admission\n- **Behavior**: Pod rejected; user sees \"Insufficient memory\" error\n- **Recovery**: Similar to CPU; add capacity or reduce requests\n\n#### Device Plugin Failures\n- **Scenario**: Device plugin crashes or becomes unresponsive\n- **Detection**: Health check timeout in device manager\n- **Behavior**: Device manager marks plugin as unhealthy; stops allocating resources\n- **Recovery**: Plugin must be restarted (usually by container orchestration)\n\n#### Cgroup v2 Kernel Incompatibility\n- **Scenario**: Kernel doesn't support required cgroup v2 features\n- **Example**: root `cpu.stat` only in kernel 5.8+\n- **Detection**: At container manager startup\n- **Behavior**: Warning issued (see `container_manager.go:57-58`); some enforcement may not work\n- **Impact**: CPU limits may not be enforced correctly\n\n#### State File Corruption\n- **Scenario**: `cpu_manager_state` or `memory_manager_state` corrupted\n- **Detection**: JSON unmarshal failure during manager startup\n- **Behavior**: Manager fails to start; kubelet refuses to start (safe fail)\n- **Recovery**: Admin must delete corrupted state files; kubelet will rebuild state\n\n#### Node Reboot with Live Containers\n- **Scenario**: Kubelet restarted but containers still running\n- **Recovery**: `buildContainerMapAndRunningSetFromRuntime()` rebuilds state from runtime\n- **Limitation**: If state file missing, kubelet may re-allocate same resources → conflicts\n- **Mitigation**: State persisted to disk; kubelet recovers from it\n\n### 4.2 Limits and Constraints\n\n#### Maximum NUMA Nodes\n- **Limit**: 8 NUMA nodes (topology manager hard limit)\n- **Reason**: Exponential state explosion in topology hint generation\n- **Code**: `topologymanager.go:41`\n- **Impact**: Machines with >8 NUMA nodes cannot use topology manager\n\n#### Maximum Concurrent Device Plugins\n- **Limit**: No explicit limit; each plugin requires dedicated goroutine\n- **Risk**: Resource exhaustion if hundreds of plugins registered\n- **Mitigation**: Practical limit ~20-30 plugins before CPU overhead significant\n\n#### PID Limits per Pod\n- **Enforced via**: `--pod-pids-limit` flag (default: none)\n- **Mechanism**: cgroup v1 pids.max or cgroup v2 pids.max\n- **Behavior**: Once hit, pod cannot spawn new processes; containers become unresponsive\n\n#### Memory Overcommit\n- **By Design**: cgroups allow setting memory.limit > node capacity\n- **Risk**: OOM killer may evict any container regardless of QoS\n- **Mitigation**: Memory manager and admissioncontroller prevent over-allocation\n- **Failure Mode**: If limits set incorrectly, random containers killed\n\n#### CPU CFS Quota Precision\n- **Granularity**: ~1 millisecond (cfs_period_us / cfs_quota_us)\n- **Issue**: Very small CPU requests (<100m) may round to 0 quota\n- **Workaround**: `cpu-cfs-quota-period` flag (default 100ms); larger = coarser\n\n### 4.3 Design Tradeoffs\n\n#### Tradeoff 1: Pre-allocation vs Post-allocation\n- **Pre-allocation** (used): CPU & memory allocated at pod admission\n  - **Pro**: Guaranteed availability; prevents overcommit\n  - **Con**: Fragmentation; reserved but unused resources\n  - **Alternative**: Post-allocation on container start would reduce fragmentation but lose guarantees\n\n#### Tradeoff 2: State Persistence\n- **Current**: State files (`cpu_manager_state`) persisted to disk\n  - **Pro**: Survives kubelet restarts; no CPU leaks\n  - **Con**: Disk I/O overhead; state drift if runtime inconsistent\n  - **Alternative**: In-memory only (faster) but loses recovery capability\n\n#### Tradeoff 3: Topology Manager Policy Strictness\n- **Policies Available**:\n  - **none**: No enforcement; allows suboptimal affinity\n  - **best-effort**: Tries optimal but allows suboptimal as fallback\n  - **restricted**: Rejects suboptimal allocations → fails pod admission\n  - **single-numa-node**: Forces all resources on one node or reject\n- **Tradeoff**: Stricter = better latency but more pod rejections\n\n#### Tradeoff 4: Cgroup Version Complexity\n- **v1**: Multiple hierarchies; per-resource config; complex but proven\n- **v2**: Unified hierarchy; simpler config; but newer kernel requirement\n- **Decision**: Support both; auto-detect; v1 being deprecated (warnings issued)\n\n#### Tradeoff 5: Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA)\n- **Traditional**: Static requests in pod spec; known at admission time\n- **DRA**: Dynamic claims; allocated at runtime; more flexible\n- **Tradeoff**: Flexibility vs complexity; DRA adds separate manager and checkpoint overhead\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 5.1 CPU Manager Policies (`pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/`)\n\n**Custom Policy Implementation**:\n\n```go\n// User can implement custom cpumanager.Policy interface\ntype Policy interface {\n    Start()                 // Initialize\n    Allocate()              // Called at pod admission\n    AddContainer()          // Called at container start\n    RemoveContainer()       // Called at container stop\n    GetTopologyHints()      // Return NUMA affinity preferences\n    GetAllocatableCPUs()    // Report allocatable CPUs\n}\n```\n\n**Limitations**:\n- Policy must be compiled into kubelet binary (no dynamic loading)\n- Register policy in `cpumanager.NewManager()` switch statement\n\n**Example**: Existing policies (none, static) show pattern for custom allocation logic.\n\n### 5.2 Memory Manager Policies (`pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/`)\n\n**Custom Policy Implementation**:\n\n```go\ntype Policy interface {\n    Start()                 // Initialize with machine topology\n    Allocate()              // Called at pod admission\n    AddContainer()          // Called at container start\n    RemoveContainer()        // Called at container stop\n    GetTopologyHints()      // Return NUMA affinity preferences\n}\n```\n\n**Current Policies**:\n- **none**: No NUMA affinity\n- **static**: Reserve memory per NUMA node\n- **best-effort**: Attempt NUMA affinity but don't fail admission\n\n### 5.3 Device Plugin System (`pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/plugin/`)\n\n**Device Plugin Registration**:\n1. Plugin listens on `/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/<plugin-name>.sock`\n2. Kubelet discovers via file watch\n3. Plugin implements `v1beta1.DevicePluginService` gRPC:\n   ```proto\n   service DevicePluginService {\n       rpc GetDevicePluginOptions()\n       rpc ListAndWatch()           // Stream devices\n       rpc Allocate()               // Called at container start\n       rpc GetPreferredAllocation() // Return NUMA hints\n       rpc PreStartContainer()      // Called before container start\n   }\n   ```\n\n**Extension Points**:\n- Custom device types (GPUs, FPGAs, custom accelerators)\n- Health monitoring (devices can report as unhealthy)\n- NUMA topology reporting (devices can advertise topology affinity)\n- Pre-start hooks (plugins can perform init on container before it starts)\n\n**Risks**:\n- Plugin crashes cause resource leaks (must manually recover state)\n- Plugins with incorrect gRPC implementation cause kubelet hangs\n- No version negotiation; breaking changes cause incompatibility\n\n### 5.4 Topology Manager Policies (`pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/`)\n\n**Bundled Policies** (cannot be extended without code change):\n- **none**: No topology coordination\n- **best-effort**: Attempts to find single NUMA node; accepts partial affinity\n- **restricted**: Requires all resources on single NUMA or rejects\n- **single-numa-node**: Strict single NUMA node requirement\n\n**Custom Hint Provider Integration**:\n\n```go\ntype HintProvider interface {\n    GetTopologyHints(pod, container)    // Return NUMA affinity hints\n    Allocate(pod, container)             // Execute allocation with selected affinity\n}\n```\n\n**How to Add Custom Resource Manager**:\n1. Implement `HintProvider` interface\n2. Call `topologyManager.AddHintProvider()` during container manager setup\n3. Manager participates in topology coordination automatically\n\n### 5.5 Pod Admission Handlers\n\n**Current Handlers** (in container manager):\n```go\n// Part of ContainerManager interface\nGetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler() lifecycle.PodAdmitHandler\n```\n\n**Implementation** wraps topology manager's admission logic.\n\n**Extension Opportunity**:\n- User can wrap the returned handler to add custom admission logic\n- Handler can reject pods based on custom resource constraints\n\n### 5.6 Internal Container Lifecycle Hooks (`pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go`)\n\n**Current Hooks**:\n- `PreCreateContainer()`: Before runtime creates container\n- `PreStartContainer()`: After creation but before start\n- `PostStopContainer()`: After container stops\n\n**User Extension**:\n- Wrap `internalContainerLifecycleImpl` to add logging, metrics, or custom resource setup\n- Must call original methods to maintain CPU/memory/topology registration\n\n### 5.7 Runtime Service Interface (`pkg/kubelet/container/runtime.go:70-150`)\n\n**Lower-level extension point**: Container manager calls runtime service methods:\n- `UpdateContainerResources()`: Update CPU/memory limits post-creation (used by CPU/memory managers)\n- `UpdatePodCIDR()`: Update networking (called by container manager)\n\n**Customization**: Replace `runtimeService` implementation to intercept/modify resource updates.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Performance Considerations\n\n#### CPU Manager Overhead\n- **Reconciliation Frequency**: Default 5 seconds (configurable)\n- **Cost**: Per-container UpdateContainerResources() RPC to runtime\n- **Impact**: With 1000 containers, reconciliation every 5s = 200 RPCs/sec to runtime\n- **Optimization**: Increase reconciliation period for large clusters; skip if no changes\n\n#### Memory Manager State Growth\n- **State File Size**: O(pods × containers)\n- **Typical**: 1KB per container; 1000 pods = ~10MB state file\n- **Disk I/O**: Persisted on every allocate/remove; can stress storage on frequent pod churn\n- **Mitigation**: Use fast storage; consider in-memory caches\n\n#### Device Manager Checkpointing\n- **Checkpoint Frequency**: On every device allocation/deallocation\n- **Risk**: With many device plugins, checkpoint overhead becomes significant\n- **Monitoring**: Watch kubelet CPU usage during pod creation surge\n\n#### Topology Manager Hint Complexity\n- **Exponential in NUMA nodes**: 2^NUMA_NODES possibilities to evaluate\n- **Impact**: With 8 NUMA nodes, generating hints for 3-pod resource types (CPU, memory, device) can take 10-50ms\n- **Mitigation**: Reduce NUMA nodes or use \"none\" policy in small topologies\n\n### 6.2 Reliability and Recovery\n\n#### Graceful Degradation on Missing State Files\n- **Behavior**: If CPU/memory manager state corrupted, kubelet refuses to start (safe fail)\n- **Recovery**: Admin must delete state files (`~/.kubelet/cpu_manager_state`, `~/.kubelet/memory_manager_state`)\n- **Consequence**: Next kubelet start rebuilds state from running containers; some allocations may be lost\n- **Best Practice**: Back up state files before kubelet upgrades\n\n#### Device Plugin Failure Handling\n- **Detection**: Health checker timeout (default 30s)\n- **Action**: Device plugin marked unhealthy; stops accepting allocations\n- **User Impact**: New pods cannot request that device; stuck in pending\n- **Recovery**: Restart device plugin or restart kubelet (to clear stale allocations)\n\n#### OOM Killer Behavior\n- **Without QoS classes**: Random container killed when node memory full\n- **With Guaranteed QoS**: Guaranteed pods protected; Burstable/BestEffort killed first\n- **With Memory Manager**: NUMA node local OOM; kills containers on that node only\n- **Visibility**: OOM events appear in pod status and node events\n\n#### Cgroup Enforcement Failures\n- **Symptom**: Container running with >memory.limit (indicates bug or cgroup bug)\n- **Cause**: Kernel may allow short-lived page cache bursts beyond hard limit\n- **Detection**: cAdvisor reports actual vs limit; monitor for discrepancies\n- **Resolution**: Usually requires waiting for OOM killer; no user action\n\n### 6.3 Debugging and Observability\n\n#### Key Metrics\n\n**cAdvisor Metrics** (collected by kubelet):\n```\ncontainer_cpu_cfs_periods_total     // CPU quota cycles\ncontainer_cpu_cfs_throttled_periods_total  // Over-limit throttles\ncontainer_memory_usage_bytes        // Current memory\ncontainer_memory_max_usage_bytes    // Peak memory\n```\n\n**kubelet Metrics** (from `pkg/kubelet/metrics/`):\n```\nkubelet_cpu_manager_cpu_allocation      // CPU allocation status\nkubelet_memory_manager_memory_allocation // Memory allocation\nkubelet_device_manager_allocation_duration // Device allocation latency\nkubelet_topology_manager_admission_duration  // Topology coordination time\n```\n\n#### Logs to Monitor\n\n**CPU Manager**:\n```\n\"Container has pinned cpus\" → Container got exclusive CPUs\n\"Failed to set CPU affinity\" → CPU binding failed; check kernel support\n```\n\n**Memory Manager**:\n```\n\"Allocating memory on NUMA node X\" → Memory allocation info\n\"Memory allocation failed\" → No available memory on preferred NUMA\n```\n\n**Device Manager**:\n```\n\"Device plugin disconnected\" → Device plugin process died\n\"Allocate RPC failed\" → Device plugin returned error\n```\n\n**Topology Manager**:\n```\n\"TopologyAffinityError\" → Cannot find affinity satisfying all providers\n```\n\n#### PodResources API (Debugging Aide)\n\n**Endpoint**: `/var/lib/kubelet/pod-resources/kubelet.sock`\n\n**Usage**: Query allocated resources for pods:\n```bash\n# List CPUs and devices allocated to pod\ncurl --unix-socket /var/lib/kubelet/pod-resources/kubelet.sock \\\n  'http://localhost/v1/pods' | protoc --decode k8s.io.kubelet.v1.PodResourcesResponse -\n```\n\n**Value**: Verify CPU/memory/device allocations match expectations; identify leaks.\n\n### 6.4 Upgrade and Rollout Considerations\n\n#### State File Format Changes\n- **Risk**: Upgrading kubelet to version with different state format\n- **Mitigation**: Kubelet version must handle old format or fail safe\n- **Best Practice**: Drain node before kubelet upgrade; recreate pods on upgrade\n\n#### cgroup v1 to v2 Migration\n- **Cost**: Must redistribute pods across both cgroup types during transition\n- **Timeline**: Gradual rollout; upgrade kubelet incrementally\n- **Monitoring**: Watch for cgroup version mismatch errors\n\n#### Device Plugin API Version Negotiation\n- **Current**: v1beta1 only; no backward compatibility layer\n- **Risk**: Upgrading kubelet while device plugins are old\n- **Mitigation**: Update device plugins before kubelet (or simultaneously)\n\n#### Pod Eviction During Upgrades\n- **Scenario**: Node marked unschedulable; pods evicted for kubelet upgrade\n- **Impact**: CPU/memory allocations freed; container runtime still enforces old limits\n- **Recovery**: Graceful termination (30s grace period) gives containers time to exit\n- **Failure Mode**: Stuck container → SIGKILL after grace period\n\n---\n\n## 7. Its architecture separates concerns cleanly: the `ContainerManager` interface defines the contract with kubelet, while implementation delegates to specialized managers for each resource dimension. The topology manager ensures NUMA-aware coordination, and careful state management enables recovery from restarts. Extension points exist for custom CPU/memory policies and device plugin integration, but the system's complexity warrants operator understanding of cgroup hierarchies, NUMA topologies, and resource reservation semantics.\n\n**Key Takeaway**: Container manager is not just a proxy to the runtime—it's an opinionated resource orchestrator that must maintain invariants (no double-allocation, QoS ordering, NUMA affinity) across pod lifecycle events and kubelet restarts. Operators must understand these invariants and potential failure modes (state corruption, device plugin failures, cgroup enforcement gaps) to troubleshoot reliably.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2764,"cache_read_input_tokens":93072,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2764},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"0a0ae5ab-3b95-43ac-98e8-0236731ee976","uuid":"a0eb5f12-efc0-40b7-b467-52514b2be85a"}

Subsystem Purpose and Scope\n\nThe **Container Manager (CM)** subsystem is responsible for managing containerized workloads on a Kubernetes node. It serves as the authoritative interface between the kubelet and the underlying container runtime infrastructure, enforcing resource constraints, managing cgroup hierarchies, and coordinating resource allocation across CPUs, memory, and specialized devices.\n\n### Core Responsibilities\n\n- **Container Lifecycle Management**: Coordinate container creation, starting, stopping, and removal through the container runtime\n- **Resource Enforcement**: Apply CPU, memory, and device limits via cgroups (v1 and v2)\n- **QoS Hierarchy**: Implement Kubernetes QoS classes (Guaranteed, Burstable, BestEffort) using cgroup hierarchies\n- **Node Allocatable**: Reserve resources for system daemons and kubelet itself\n- **Resource Coordination**: Orchestrate allocation decisions across CPU manager, memory manager, device manager, and topology manager\n- **Health Checking**: Monitor device plugins and report resource health status\n\n### Boundaries and Upstream/Downstream Dependencies\n\n**Upstream Dependencies (Callers):**\n- **Kubelet (`pkg/kubelet/kubelet.go`)**: Calls CM to initialize, manage pod lifecycle, and enforce node allocatable\n- **Pod Workers (`pkg/kubelet/pod_workers.go`)**: Requests container runtime operations via CM\n- **Lifecycle Hooks**: Pod admission handlers and resource allocation triggers\n- **API Server**: Provides pod and node specifications\n\n**Downstream Dependencies (Consumers):**\n- **Container Runtime Interface (CRI)**: gRPC service for container/sandbox operations\n- **cgroup Filesystem**: Linux kernel interface for resource enforcement\n- **Device Plugins**: Kubernetes device plugin protocol for custom resources\n- **OOM Killer & Kernel**: Linux kernel mechanisms for resource enforcement and OOM handling\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 Core Container Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/`)\n\n**Main Interface: `ContainerManager` (`container_manager.go:66-170`)**\n\nThe primary abstraction defining the contract for all CM operations:\n\n```\ntype ContainerManager interface {\n    Start()                              // Initialize and verify system state\n    SystemCgroupsLimit()                 // Reserve resources for system\n    GetNodeConfig()                      // Access configuration\n    NewPodContainerManager()             // Factory for pod-level cgroup manager\n    GetResources()                       // Resolve extended resources for pods\n    InternalContainerLifecycle()         // Register lifecycle hooks\n    GetPluginRegistrationHandlers()      // Support device plugin discovery\n    UpdateQOSCgroups()                   // Periodic housekeeping\n    GetCapacity()                        // Report node capacity\n    GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()// Pod admission hook\n    PrepareDynamicResources()            // DRA resource preparation\n    // ... and many more methods\n}\n```\n\n**Implementation: `containerManagerImpl` (`container_manager_linux.go:100-140`)**\n\nThe Linux-specific implementation holding:\n\n- **cgroup manager** (`cgroupManager CgroupManager`): Manages cgroup hierarchy creation/updates via systemd or cgroupfs\n- **Resource managers**: CPU, memory, device, topology, and DRA managers\n- **QoS container manager** (`qosContainerManager QOSContainerManager`): Maintains Guaranteed/Burstable/BestEffort hierarchy\n- **Periodic tasks**: Background jobs for reconciliation and enforcement\n\n### 2.2 cgroup Management (`pkg/kubelet/cm/`)\n\n**Cgroup Manager Interface (`types.go:62-97`)**\n\nAbstracts cgroup operations:\n\n```\ntype CgroupManager interface {\n    Create()              // Create cgroup with resource limits\n    Destroy()             // Remove cgroup\n    Update()              // Modify resource limits\n    Exists()              // Check cgroup presence\n    GetCgroupConfig()     // Read applied resource config\n    MemoryUsage()         // Query current memory consumption\n    Pids()                // List processes in cgroup\n    ReduceCPULimits()     // Hard-cap CPU shares\n    Version()             // Return cgroup version (1 or 2)\n}\n```\n\n**cgroup Hierarchy Structure:**\n\n```\n/ (root)\n├── system.slice/          (--system-reserved-cgroups)\n├── kubepods.slice/        (Pod cgroup root, --pod-cgroup-root)\n│   ├── guaranteed/        (Guaranteed QoS class)\n│   │   └── pod<uid>/      (Individual pods)\n│   │       ├── <container> (Actual containers)\n│   ├── burstable/         (Burstable QoS class)\n│   │   └── pod<uid>/\n│   └── besteffort/        (BestEffort QoS class)\n│       └── pod<uid>/\n└── docker/                (System container for kubelet)\n    └── <pid> -> actual kubelet process\n```\n\n**Cgroup Versions (v1 vs v2):**\n- **v1** (`cgroup_manager_linux.go`): Separate hierarchies per resource type (cpu, memory, cpuset)\n- **v2** (`cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go`): Unified hierarchy with unified cgroup config\n- Detected at runtime; v1 deprecated (see warning at `container_manager.go:52`)\n\n### 2.3 Resource Managers\n\n#### CPU Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/`)\n\n**Purpose**: Allocate exclusive CPUs for latency-sensitive workloads.\n\n**Key Methods** (`cpu_manager.go:55-103`):\n- `Allocate()`: Pre-allocate CPUs at pod admission time\n- `AddContainer()`: Register container after creation; apply CPU affinity\n- `RemoveContainer()`: Free CPUs when container stops\n- `GetTopologyHints()`: Provide NUMA affinity preferences\n- `GetExclusiveCPUs()`: Query assigned CPUs (PodResources API)\n\n**Policies**:\n- **none** (`policy_none.go`): No CPU affinity; shared pool\n- **static** (`policy_static.go`): Exclusive CPU allocation for QoS=Guaranteed pods; others share\n- Policy state stored in `cpu_manager_state` file under kubelet root dir\n\n#### Memory Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/`)\n\n**Purpose**: Allocate memory from specific NUMA nodes (memory affinity).\n\n**Key Methods** (`memory_manager.go:57-95`):\n- `Allocate()`: Pre-allocate memory at pod admission\n- `AddContainer()`: Apply NUMA memory binding after container creation\n- `RemoveContainer()`: Release NUMA memory reservation\n- `GetTopologyHints()`: Provide NUMA affinity preferences\n- `GetMemoryNUMANodes()`: Query assigned NUMA nodes\n\n**Policies**:\n- **none**: No NUMA affinity; memory from any node\n- **static**: Reserve memory from specific NUMA nodes; allocate from reserved pools\n- State stored in `memory_manager_state` file\n\n#### Device Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/`)\n\n**Purpose**: Manage extended resources (GPUs, NICs) provided by device plugins.\n\n**Key Components** (`manager.go:61-100`):\n- **endpoints**: Tracks registered device plugins\n- **allocatedDevices**: Per-pod device allocations\n- **topologyAffinityStore**: NUMA topology for devices\n- **checkpointManager**: Persists allocation state\n\n**Workflow**:\n1. Device plugin registers via Unix socket\n2. Plugin reports available device IDs\n3. Kubelet allocates devices to pods (Allocate() call)\n4. Device manager returns device env vars, mounts, and CDI devices\n5. Kubelet passes these to container runtime\n\n#### Topology Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/`)\n\n**Purpose**: Coordinate resource affinity across CPU, memory, and device managers.\n\n**Key Concepts**:\n- **Scopes**: pod (single pod) or container (per-container)\n- **Policies**: none, best-effort, restricted, single-numa-node\n- **Hint Provider Interface**: CPU, memory, device managers implement to provide topology hints\n- **Affinity Resolution**: Merges hints from all providers to find best NUMA node set\n\n**Flow**:\n1. Pod admission triggers topology manager's PodAdmitHandler\n2. Queries all hint providers (CPU, memory, device managers)\n3. Merges hints to find consensus best affinity\n4. Stores affinity result; providers retrieve via GetAffinity()\n5. Providers allocate resources accordingly\n\n#### DRA Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/`)\n\n**Purpose**: Manage Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) claims and per-node resources.\n\n**Integration**: Manages allocation of DRAClaims to pods; coordinates with device manager.\n\n### 2.4 Pod Container Management (`pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_*.go`)\n\n**Interface: `PodContainerManager` (`types.go:106-141`)**\n\nManages pod-level cgroup containers (when QoS hierarchy enabled):\n\n```\ntype PodContainerManager interface {\n    GetPodContainerName()           // Get cgroup name for pod\n    EnsureExists()                  // Create pod cgroup if needed\n    Exists()                        // Check pod cgroup presence\n    Destroy()                       // Remove pod cgroup\n    GetAllPodsFromCgroups()         // Enumerate existing pods\n    IsPodCgroup()                   // Identify if path is pod cgroup\n    GetPodCgroupMemoryUsage()       // Query memory consumption\n    // ... and others\n}\n```\n\n**Implementation: `podContainerManagerImpl` (when `--cgroups-per-qos=true`)**\n- Creates pod-level cgroups under QoS class containers\n- Applies CPU, memory, and PID limits based on pod requests\n- Enforces memory QoS limits (cgroup v2 only)\n\n**Fallback: `podContainerManagerNoop` (when `--cgroups-per-qos=false`)**\n- No-op implementation; pods share QoS class cgroups\n\n### 2.5 QoS Container Manager (`pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_linux.go`)\n\n**Purpose**: Create and manage top-level QoS class cgroup hierarchy.\n\n**Initialization** (`qos_container_manager_linux.go:84-130`):\n1. Creates three top-level cgroup containers:\n   - `kubepods/guaranteed` (for Guaranteed pods)\n   - `kubepods/burstable` (for Burstable pods)\n   - `kubepods/besteffort` (for BestEffort pods)\n2. Sets CPU shares and memory limits based on node allocatable\n3. Periodic reconciliation via `UpdateCgroups()`\n\n### 2.6 Internal Container Lifecycle (`pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go`)\n\n**Purpose**: Hook container lifecycle events to resource managers.\n\n**Methods** (`internal_container_lifecycle.go:28-57`):\n\n```\ntype InternalContainerLifecycle interface {\n    PreCreateContainer()   // Before runtime creates container\n    PreStartContainer()    // Before container starts (after creation)\n    PostStopContainer()    // After container stops\n}\n```\n\n**Implementation** (`internalContainerLifecycleImpl`):\n- `PreStartContainer()`: Calls CPU and memory managers' AddContainer()\n- `PostStopContainer()`: Calls topology manager's RemoveContainer()\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### 3.1 Container Manager Initialization (`container_manager_linux.go:615-650+`)\n\n**Entry Point**: `containerManagerImpl.Start()` (kubelet startup)\n\n**Sequence**:\n\n```\nStart(ctx, node, activePods, getNode, sourcesReady, podStatusProvider, runtimeService)\n  ↓\n1. buildContainerMapAndRunningSetFromRuntime()\n   - Query runtime for existing containers\n   - Build map of active containers before kubelet restart\n\n2. setupNode()\n   - Validate cgroup subsystems available\n   - Check kernel tunables (VM overcommit, panic on OOM, etc.)\n   - Create node allocatable cgroup if --cgroups-per-qos=true\n   - Start QOS container manager\n   - Set up system containers (system.slice, docker)\n\n3. Start DRA manager (if DynamicResourceAllocation feature enabled)\n\n4. Start CPU manager\n   - Initialize CPU topology from cAdvisor\n   - Load persisted state from cpu_manager_state\n   - Start reconciliation goroutine\n\n5. Start memory manager\n   - Load persisted state from memory_manager_state\n   - Initialize NUMA node mapping\n   - Start reconciliation goroutine\n\n6. Create unified resource updates channel\n   - Fan-in device manager and DRA manager updates\n   - Kubelet main loop consumes this channel\n\n7. Register device manager as hint provider with topology manager\n8. Register CPU manager as hint provider with topology manager\n9. Register memory manager as hint provider with topology manager\n```\n\n### 3.2 Pod Admission and Resource Allocation\n\n**Entry Point**: Pod created in API server → kubelet watches → pod workers process\n\n**Sequence**:\n\n```\nkubelet.podWorkers.UpdatePod(pod)\n  ↓\nGenerateAPIPodStatus()\n  ↓\ncontainerManager.UpdatePluginResources()\n  - Call device manager to update node allocatable with device plugin resources\n  ↓\ncontainerManager.GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()\n  ↓\nhandler.Admit(pod)\n  ↓\ntopologyManager.Admit(pod)\n  ↓\nFor each container in pod:\n  1. cpuManager.GetTopologyHints()     → {cpu: [numa0:true, numa1:false]}\n  2. memoryManager.GetTopologyHints()  → {memory: [numa0:true, numa1:false]}\n  3. deviceManager.GetTopologyHints()  → {gpu: [numa0:true]}\n  ↓\n  Merge hints → {numa0: preferred}\n  ↓\n4. cpuManager.Allocate(pod, container)\n   - If static policy + QoS=Guaranteed:\n     - Reserve exclusive CPUs from cpuManager.cpuset\n     - Save to state file\n   - Else: shared pool (no pre-allocation)\n\n5. memoryManager.Allocate(pod, container)\n   - If static policy + sufficient memory on preferred NUMA:\n     - Reserve memory from that node's pool\n     - Save to state file\n   - Else: no NUMA affinity\n\n6. deviceManager.Allocate(pod)\n   - Call device plugin's Allocate() RPC\n   - Device plugin returns device IDs and mount/env info\n   - Save allocation to checkpoint\n```\n\n### 3.3 Container Creation and Start\n\n**Entry Point**: Pod sync in pod worker\n\n**Sequence**:\n\n```\nkuberuntime_manager.SyncPod(pod, ...)\n  ↓\nFor each init/regular container:\n\n1. kuberuntime_container.createContainer()\n   ↓\n   containerManager.GetResources(pod, container)\n   - Topology manager returns selected NUMA affinity\n   - CPU manager returns exclusive CPUs (if any)\n   - Memory manager returns NUMA memory binding\n   - Device manager returns mounts, env, CDI devices\n   - Return RunContainerOptions with all above\n   ↓\n   runtimeService.CreateContainer(config)\n   - Include RunContainerOptions in CRI request\n   - Runtime (containerd/CRI-O) creates sandbox/container with cgroups\n\n2. containerManager.InternalContainerLifecycle().PreStartContainer()\n   ↓\n   cpuManager.AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n   - Apply CPU affinity via UpdateContainerResources() RPC\n   - If exclusive CPUs: TaskSet the container\n   - Record in cpuManager state\n   ↓\n   memoryManager.AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n   - Apply NUMA memory binding\n   - Record in memoryManager state\n   ↓\n   topologyManager.AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n   - Store affinity → enable future queries via PodResources API\n\n3. runtimeService.StartContainer(containerID)\n   - Container actually runs with applied resource constraints\n```\n\n### 3.4 Container Cleanup\n\n**Entry Point**: Pod deletion or container failure\n\n**Sequence**:\n\n```\nkuberuntime_manager.KillPod() or KillContainer()\n  ↓\nruntimeService.StopContainer(containerID)\n  - Container stops\n\ncontainerManager.InternalContainerLifecycle().PostStopContainer()\n  ↓\ntopologyManager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n  - Forget topology affinity\n\n(No explicit CPU/memory manager cleanup; tracked via containerID)\n\ncpuManager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n  - Free exclusive CPUs\n  - Update cpuManager state\n\nmemoryManager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n  - Free NUMA memory reservation\n  - Update memoryManager state\n\ndeviceManager tracks containers and cleans up on pod deletion\n  - Update checkpoint file\n```\n\n### 3.5 Periodic Reconciliation\n\n**Triggered by**: Timer in each resource manager\n\n**CPU Manager Reconciliation** (default 5s):\n```\ncpuManager.reconcileState()\n  ↓\n1. Get list of active pods from kubelet\n2. Compare with cpuManager state\n3. For containers no longer in active pods:\n   - Remove from state\n   - Free CPUs\n4. For containers in state but not in runtime:\n   - Try to recover via runtime.GetContainers()\n5. For containers with wrong CPU affinity:\n   - Call UpdateContainerResources() to fix\n6. Save state to disk\n```\n\n**Memory Manager Reconciliation** (similar pattern):\n```\nmemoryManager.reconcileState()\n  ↓\n1. Validate allocations against runtime containers\n2. Free allocations for dead pods\n3. Save state to disk\n```\n\n**QoS Manager Reconciliation** (default 1 minute):\n```\nqosContainerManager.UpdateCgroups()\n  ↓\n1. Recompute expected CPU/memory for each QoS class\n2. Get list of active pods in each QoS class\n3. Update cgroup limits to match current allocation + reserved\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Failure Modes\n\n#### CPU Allocation Conflicts\n- **Scenario**: Pod with `requests.cpu` exceeds allocatable non-reserved CPUs\n- **Detection**: cpuManager.Allocate() fails during pod admission\n- **Behavior**: Pod rejected; user sees \"Insufficient cpu\" error\n- **Recovery**: User must reduce pod CPU request or add more nodes\n\n#### Memory Allocation Failures\n- **Scenario**: Pod with NUMA memory affinity but all NUMA nodes exhausted\n- **Detection**: memoryManager.Allocate() fails during pod admission\n- **Behavior**: Pod rejected; user sees \"Insufficient memory\" error\n- **Recovery**: Similar to CPU; add capacity or reduce requests\n\n#### Device Plugin Failures\n- **Scenario**: Device plugin crashes or becomes unresponsive\n- **Detection**: Health check timeout in device manager\n- **Behavior**: Device manager marks plugin as unhealthy; stops allocating resources\n- **Recovery**: Plugin must be restarted (usually by container orchestration)\n\n#### Cgroup v2 Kernel Incompatibility\n- **Scenario**: Kernel doesn't support required cgroup v2 features\n- **Example**: root `cpu.stat` only in kernel 5.8+\n- **Detection**: At container manager startup\n- **Behavior**: Warning issued (see `container_manager.go:57-58`); some enforcement may not work\n- **Impact**: CPU limits may not be enforced correctly\n\n#### State File Corruption\n- **Scenario**: `cpu_manager_state` or `memory_manager_state` corrupted\n- **Detection**: JSON unmarshal failure during manager startup\n- **Behavior**: Manager fails to start; kubelet refuses to start (safe fail)\n- **Recovery**: Admin must delete corrupted state files; kubelet will rebuild state\n\n#### Node Reboot with Live Containers\n- **Scenario**: Kubelet restarted but containers still running\n- **Recovery**: `buildContainerMapAndRunningSetFromRuntime()` rebuilds state from runtime\n- **Limitation**: If state file missing, kubelet may re-allocate same resources → conflicts\n- **Mitigation**: State persisted to disk; kubelet recovers from it\n\n### 4.2 Limits and Constraints\n\n#### Maximum NUMA Nodes\n- **Limit**: 8 NUMA nodes (topology manager hard limit)\n- **Reason**: Exponential state explosion in topology hint generation\n- **Code**: `topologymanager.go:41`\n- **Impact**: Machines with >8 NUMA nodes cannot use topology manager\n\n#### Maximum Concurrent Device Plugins\n- **Limit**: No explicit limit; each plugin requires dedicated goroutine\n- **Risk**: Resource exhaustion if hundreds of plugins registered\n- **Mitigation**: Practical limit ~20-30 plugins before CPU overhead significant\n\n#### PID Limits per Pod\n- **Enforced via**: `--pod-pids-limit` flag (default: none)\n- **Mechanism**: cgroup v1 pids.max or cgroup v2 pids.max\n- **Behavior**: Once hit, pod cannot spawn new processes; containers become unresponsive\n\n#### Memory Overcommit\n- **By Design**: cgroups allow setting memory.limit > node capacity\n- **Risk**: OOM killer may evict any container regardless of QoS\n- **Mitigation**: Memory manager and admissioncontroller prevent over-allocation\n- **Failure Mode**: If limits set incorrectly, random containers killed\n\n#### CPU CFS Quota Precision\n- **Granularity**: ~1 millisecond (cfs_period_us / cfs_quota_us)\n- **Issue**: Very small CPU requests (<100m) may round to 0 quota\n- **Workaround**: `cpu-cfs-quota-period` flag (default 100ms); larger = coarser\n\n### 4.3 Design Tradeoffs\n\n#### Tradeoff 1: Pre-allocation vs Post-allocation\n- **Pre-allocation** (used): CPU & memory allocated at pod admission\n  - **Pro**: Guaranteed availability; prevents overcommit\n  - **Con**: Fragmentation; reserved but unused resources\n  - **Alternative**: Post-allocation on container start would reduce fragmentation but lose guarantees\n\n#### Tradeoff 2: State Persistence\n- **Current**: State files (`cpu_manager_state`) persisted to disk\n  - **Pro**: Survives kubelet restarts; no CPU leaks\n  - **Con**: Disk I/O overhead; state drift if runtime inconsistent\n  - **Alternative**: In-memory only (faster) but loses recovery capability\n\n#### Tradeoff 3: Topology Manager Policy Strictness\n- **Policies Available**:\n  - **none**: No enforcement; allows suboptimal affinity\n  - **best-effort**: Tries optimal but allows suboptimal as fallback\n  - **restricted**: Rejects suboptimal allocations → fails pod admission\n  - **single-numa-node**: Forces all resources on one node or reject\n- **Tradeoff**: Stricter = better latency but more pod rejections\n\n#### Tradeoff 4: Cgroup Version Complexity\n- **v1**: Multiple hierarchies; per-resource config; complex but proven\n- **v2**: Unified hierarchy; simpler config; but newer kernel requirement\n- **Decision**: Support both; auto-detect; v1 being deprecated (warnings issued)\n\n#### Tradeoff 5: Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA)\n- **Traditional**: Static requests in pod spec; known at admission time\n- **DRA**: Dynamic claims; allocated at runtime; more flexible\n- **Tradeoff**: Flexibility vs complexity; DRA adds separate manager and checkpoint overhead\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 5.1 CPU Manager Policies (`pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/`)\n\n**Custom Policy Implementation**:\n\n```go\n// User can implement custom cpumanager.Policy interface\ntype Policy interface {\n    Start()                 // Initialize\n    Allocate()              // Called at pod admission\n    AddContainer()          // Called at container start\n    RemoveContainer()       // Called at container stop\n    GetTopologyHints()      // Return NUMA affinity preferences\n    GetAllocatableCPUs()    // Report allocatable CPUs\n}\n```\n\n**Limitations**:\n- Policy must be compiled into kubelet binary (no dynamic loading)\n- Register policy in `cpumanager.NewManager()` switch statement\n\n**Example**: Existing policies (none, static) show pattern for custom allocation logic.\n\n### 5.2 Memory Manager Policies (`pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/`)\n\n**Custom Policy Implementation**:\n\n```go\ntype Policy interface {\n    Start()                 // Initialize with machine topology\n    Allocate()              // Called at pod admission\n    AddContainer()          // Called at container start\n    RemoveContainer()        // Called at container stop\n    GetTopologyHints()      // Return NUMA affinity preferences\n}\n```\n\n**Current Policies**:\n- **none**: No NUMA affinity\n- **static**: Reserve memory per NUMA node\n- **best-effort**: Attempt NUMA affinity but don't fail admission\n\n### 5.3 Device Plugin System (`pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/plugin/`)\n\n**Device Plugin Registration**:\n1. Plugin listens on `/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/<plugin-name>.sock`\n2. Kubelet discovers via file watch\n3. Plugin implements `v1beta1.DevicePluginService` gRPC:\n   ```proto\n   service DevicePluginService {\n       rpc GetDevicePluginOptions()\n       rpc ListAndWatch()           // Stream devices\n       rpc Allocate()               // Called at container start\n       rpc GetPreferredAllocation() // Return NUMA hints\n       rpc PreStartContainer()      // Called before container start\n   }\n   ```\n\n**Extension Points**:\n- Custom device types (GPUs, FPGAs, custom accelerators)\n- Health monitoring (devices can report as unhealthy)\n- NUMA topology reporting (devices can advertise topology affinity)\n- Pre-start hooks (plugins can perform init on container before it starts)\n\n**Risks**:\n- Plugin crashes cause resource leaks (must manually recover state)\n- Plugins with incorrect gRPC implementation cause kubelet hangs\n- No version negotiation; breaking changes cause incompatibility\n\n### 5.4 Topology Manager Policies (`pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/`)\n\n**Bundled Policies** (cannot be extended without code change):\n- **none**: No topology coordination\n- **best-effort**: Attempts to find single NUMA node; accepts partial affinity\n- **restricted**: Requires all resources on single NUMA or rejects\n- **single-numa-node**: Strict single NUMA node requirement\n\n**Custom Hint Provider Integration**:\n\n```go\ntype HintProvider interface {\n    GetTopologyHints(pod, container)    // Return NUMA affinity hints\n    Allocate(pod, container)             // Execute allocation with selected affinity\n}\n```\n\n**How to Add Custom Resource Manager**:\n1. Implement `HintProvider` interface\n2. Call `topologyManager.AddHintProvider()` during container manager setup\n3. Manager participates in topology coordination automatically\n\n### 5.5 Pod Admission Handlers\n\n**Current Handlers** (in container manager):\n```go\n// Part of ContainerManager interface\nGetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler() lifecycle.PodAdmitHandler\n```\n\n**Implementation** wraps topology manager's admission logic.\n\n**Extension Opportunity**:\n- User can wrap the returned handler to add custom admission logic\n- Handler can reject pods based on custom resource constraints\n\n### 5.6 Internal Container Lifecycle Hooks (`pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go`)\n\n**Current Hooks**:\n- `PreCreateContainer()`: Before runtime creates container\n- `PreStartContainer()`: After creation but before start\n- `PostStopContainer()`: After container stops\n\n**User Extension**:\n- Wrap `internalContainerLifecycleImpl` to add logging, metrics, or custom resource setup\n- Must call original methods to maintain CPU/memory/topology registration\n\n### 5.7 Runtime Service Interface (`pkg/kubelet/container/runtime.go:70-150`)\n\n**Lower-level extension point**: Container manager calls runtime service methods:\n- `UpdateContainerResources()`: Update CPU/memory limits post-creation (used by CPU/memory managers)\n- `UpdatePodCIDR()`: Update networking (called by container manager)\n\n**Customization**: Replace `runtimeService` implementation to intercept/modify resource updates.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Performance Considerations\n\n#### CPU Manager Overhead\n- **Reconciliation Frequency**: Default 5 seconds (configurable)\n- **Cost**: Per-container UpdateContainerResources() RPC to runtime\n- **Impact**: With 1000 containers, reconciliation every 5s = 200 RPCs/sec to runtime\n- **Optimization**: Increase reconciliation period for large clusters; skip if no changes\n\n#### Memory Manager State Growth\n- **State File Size**: O(pods × containers)\n- **Typical**: 1KB per container; 1000 pods = ~10MB state file\n- **Disk I/O**: Persisted on every allocate/remove; can stress storage on frequent pod churn\n- **Mitigation**: Use fast storage; consider in-memory caches\n\n#### Device Manager Checkpointing\n- **Checkpoint Frequency**: On every device allocation/deallocation\n- **Risk**: With many device plugins, checkpoint overhead becomes significant\n- **Monitoring**: Watch kubelet CPU usage during pod creation surge\n\n#### Topology Manager Hint Complexity\n- **Exponential in NUMA nodes**: 2^NUMA_NODES possibilities to evaluate\n- **Impact**: With 8 NUMA nodes, generating hints for 3-pod resource types (CPU, memory, device) can take 10-50ms\n- **Mitigation**: Reduce NUMA nodes or use \"none\" policy in small topologies\n\n### 6.2 Reliability and Recovery\n\n#### Graceful Degradation on Missing State Files\n- **Behavior**: If CPU/memory manager state corrupted, kubelet refuses to start (safe fail)\n- **Recovery**: Admin must delete state files (`~/.kubelet/cpu_manager_state`, `~/.kubelet/memory_manager_state`)\n- **Consequence**: Next kubelet start rebuilds state from running containers; some allocations may be lost\n- **Best Practice**: Back up state files before kubelet upgrades\n\n#### Device Plugin Failure Handling\n- **Detection**: Health checker timeout (default 30s)\n- **Action**: Device plugin marked unhealthy; stops accepting allocations\n- **User Impact**: New pods cannot request that device; stuck in pending\n- **Recovery**: Restart device plugin or restart kubelet (to clear stale allocations)\n\n#### OOM Killer Behavior\n- **Without QoS classes**: Random container killed when node memory full\n- **With Guaranteed QoS**: Guaranteed pods protected; Burstable/BestEffort killed first\n- **With Memory Manager**: NUMA node local OOM; kills containers on that node only\n- **Visibility**: OOM events appear in pod status and node events\n\n#### Cgroup Enforcement Failures\n- **Symptom**: Container running with >memory.limit (indicates bug or cgroup bug)\n- **Cause**: Kernel may allow short-lived page cache bursts beyond hard limit\n- **Detection**: cAdvisor reports actual vs limit; monitor for discrepancies\n- **Resolution**: Usually requires waiting for OOM killer; no user action\n\n### 6.3 Debugging and Observability\n\n#### Key Metrics\n\n**cAdvisor Metrics** (collected by kubelet):\n```\ncontainer_cpu_cfs_periods_total     // CPU quota cycles\ncontainer_cpu_cfs_throttled_periods_total  // Over-limit throttles\ncontainer_memory_usage_bytes        // Current memory\ncontainer_memory_max_usage_bytes    // Peak memory\n```\n\n**kubelet Metrics** (from `pkg/kubelet/metrics/`):\n```\nkubelet_cpu_manager_cpu_allocation      // CPU allocation status\nkubelet_memory_manager_memory_allocation // Memory allocation\nkubelet_device_manager_allocation_duration // Device allocation latency\nkubelet_topology_manager_admission_duration  // Topology coordination time\n```\n\n#### Logs to Monitor\n\n**CPU Manager**:\n```\n\"Container has pinned cpus\" → Container got exclusive CPUs\n\"Failed to set CPU affinity\" → CPU binding failed; check kernel support\n```\n\n**Memory Manager**:\n```\n\"Allocating memory on NUMA node X\" → Memory allocation info\n\"Memory allocation failed\" → No available memory on preferred NUMA\n```\n\n**Device Manager**:\n```\n\"Device plugin disconnected\" → Device plugin process died\n\"Allocate RPC failed\" → Device plugin returned error\n```\n\n**Topology Manager**:\n```\n\"TopologyAffinityError\" → Cannot find affinity satisfying all providers\n```\n\n#### PodResources API (Debugging Aide)\n\n**Endpoint**: `/var/lib/kubelet/pod-resources/kubelet.sock`\n\n**Usage**: Query allocated resources for pods:\n```bash\n# List CPUs and devices allocated to pod\ncurl --unix-socket /var/lib/kubelet/pod-resources/kubelet.sock \\\n  'http://localhost/v1/pods' | protoc --decode k8s.io.kubelet.v1.PodResourcesResponse -\n```\n\n**Value**: Verify CPU/memory/device allocations match expectations; identify leaks.\n\n### 6.4 Upgrade and Rollout Considerations\n\n#### State File Format Changes\n- **Risk**: Upgrading kubelet to version with different state format\n- **Mitigation**: Kubelet version must handle old format or fail safe\n- **Best Practice**: Drain node before kubelet upgrade; recreate pods on upgrade\n\n#### cgroup v1 to v2 Migration\n- **Cost**: Must redistribute pods across both cgroup types during transition\n- **Timeline**: Gradual rollout; upgrade kubelet incrementally\n- **Monitoring**: Watch for cgroup version mismatch errors\n\n#### Device Plugin API Version Negotiation\n- **Current**: v1beta1 only; no backward compatibility layer\n- **Risk**: Upgrading kubelet while device plugins are old\n- **Mitigation**: Update device plugins before kubelet (or simultaneously)\n\n#### Pod Eviction During Upgrades\n- **Scenario**: Node marked unschedulable; pods evicted for kubelet upgrade\n- **Impact**: CPU/memory allocations freed; container runtime still enforces old limits\n- **Recovery**: Graceful termination (30s grace period) gives containers time to exit\n- **Failure Mode**: Stuck container → SIGKILL after grace period\n\n---\n\n## 7. Important Files and Directory Map\n\n### Core Container Manager\n```\npkg/kubelet/cm/\n├── container_manager.go               # ContainerManager interface definition\n├── container_manager_linux.go         # Linux implementation & initialization\n├── container_manager_windows.go       # Windows stub\n├── container_manager_unsupported.go   # Unsupported platforms\n├── types.go                            # CgroupName, CgroupConfig, interfaces\n├── helpers_linux.go                    # Cgroup path/config helpers\n└── helpers_unsupported.go\n```\n\n### cgroup Management\n```\npkg/kubelet/cm/\n├── cgroup_manager_linux.go            # cgroup manager interface implementation\n├── cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go        # cgroup v1 specific logic\n├── cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go        # cgroup v2 specific logic\n├── cgroup_manager_unsupported.go\n└── node_container_manager_linux.go   # No affinity policy\n├── policy_static.go                   # Exclusive CPU allocation\n├── cpu_manager.go:55-103              # Manager interface definition\n├── state/                             # State persistence\n│   ├── cpu_memory_state.go           # State representation\n│   └── checkpointer.go               # State file I/O\n└── topology/                          # CPU topology querying\n\npkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/\n├── memory_manager.go                  # Manager interface\n├── policy_none.go                     # No NUMA affinity\n├── policy_static.go                   # Static NUMA reservation\n├── state/                             # State persistence\n│   └── memory_blocks.go              # Memory block allocation tracking\n└── topology/                          # NUMA topology\n```\n\n### Device Management\n```\npkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/\n├── manager.go                         # Device manager implementation\n├── plugin/                            # Device plugin protocol implementation\n│   └── v1beta1/\n│       ├── api.pb.go                 # Generated gRPC stubs\n│       └── client.go                  # Device plugin client\n├── checkpoint/                        # Device allocation checkpointing\n│   ├── checkpoint.go                 # Checkpoint file format\n│   └── v1_handler.go                 # V1 checkpoint format\n├── pod_devices.go                     # Per-pod device tracking\n└── types.go                           # ResourceDeviceInstances, etc.\n```\n\n### Topology Management\n```\npkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/\n├── topology_manager.go               # Manager & HintProvider interface\n├── policy_none.go                    # No coordination\n├── policy_best_effort.go             # Best-effort single-node affinity\n├── policy_restricted.go              # Strict single-node enforcement\n├── policy_single_numa_node.go        # Single-node requirement\n├── scope.go                           # pod vs. container scope\n├── scope_pod.go                       # Pod-scoped coordination\n├── scope_container.go                # Container-scoped coordination\n├── numa_info.go                       # NUMA topology representation\n└── bitmask/                           # Topology hint bitmask operations\n```\n\n### QoS & Pod Container Management\n```\npkg/kubelet/cm/\n├── qos_container_manager_linux.go    # QoS class hierarchy setup\n├── pod_container_manager_linux.go    # Pod-level cgroups (when QoS enabled)\n├── pod_container_manager_stub.go     # Pod manager when QoS disabled\n└── internal_container_lifecycle.go   # Lifecycle hook implementation\n```\n\n### Container Runtime Interface\n```\npkg/kubelet/container/\n├── runtime.go                        # Runtime, ImageService interfaces\n├── runtime_cache.go                  # Container list caching\n├── sync_result.go                    # Pod sync result tracking\n└── cache.go                          # Container metadata caching\n\npkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/\n├── kuberuntime_manager.go            # Concrete runtime manager\n├── kuberuntime_container.go          # Container creation/start/stop\n├── kuberuntime_sandbox.go            # Pod sandbox management\n├── kuberuntime_gc.go                 # Container garbage collection\n└── instrumented_services.go          # Metrics wrapper\n```\n\n### DRA (Dynamic Resource Allocation)\n```\npkg/kubelet/cm/dra/\n├── manager.go                        # DRA manager implementation\n├── api.go                            # DRA API helpers\n└── state/                            # DRA state persistence\n```\n\n### Testing & Mocking\n```\npkg/kubelet/cm/\n├── fake_container_manager.go         # Mock for testing\n├── fake_pod_container_manager.go     # Mock pod container manager\n├── testing/\n│   └── mocks.go                      # Autogenerated mocks (mockery)\n└── [*_test.go]                       # Unit tests for all components\n\npkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/testing/\n└── fake_cpu_manager.go               # CPU manager mock\n\npkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/testing/\n└── fake_device_manager.go            # Device manager mock\n```\n\n### Configuration\n```\npkg/kubelet/apis/config/\n├── types.go                          # KubeletConfiguration struct\n├── validation/                       # Config validation\n└── defaults/                         # Default values\n```\n\n### State File Locations (at Runtime)\n\n```\n$KUBELET_ROOT_DIR/\n├── cpu_manager_state                 # CPU allocation state (JSON)\n├── memory_manager_state              # Memory allocation state (JSON)\n├── device-plugin-state/\n│   └── <plugin-name>_state           # Per-plugin device checkpoint\n├── pod-resources/\n│   └── kubelet.sock                  # PodResources API socket\n└── pods/                             # Pod volume mounts\n```\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe kubelet container manager is a sophisticated coordination layer managing resource allocation across multiple independent systems (CPU, memory, devices) while enforcing QoS hierarchies and handling platform variations. Its architecture separates concerns cleanly: the `ContainerManager` interface defines the contract with kubelet, while implementation delegates to specialized managers for each resource dimension. The topology manager ensures NUMA-aware coordination, and careful state management enables recovery from restarts. Extension points exist for custom CPU/memory policies and device plugin integration, but the system's complexity warrants operator understanding of cgroup hierarchies, NUMA topologies, and resource reservation semantics.\n\n**Key Takeaway**: Container manager is not just a proxy to the runtime—it's an opinionated resource orchestrator that must maintain invariants (no double-allocation, QoS ordering, NUMA affinity) across pod lifecycle events and kubelet restarts. Operators must understand these invariants and potential failure modes (state corruption, device plugin failures, cgroup enforcement gaps) to troubleshoot reliably.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
